Going left, right, and jumping would take up all but clapping on the bongos, which leaves only 1 action left, you can't fit punching, using an item, and wild moves on clapping. The wild moves is what I think really elevates the game, and I think that should be the basis for another Donkey Kong racing game (unless they go the Diddy Kong Racing route). It fits DK so well, it's like how rolling worked in the SNES DKC games, ramming into barrels and other racers to reset your boost, like in DKC where rolling into enemies extended your roll is a great mechanic. The game is pretty flawed, aside from the controls, the tracks aren't too interesting and repeat themes, and I think that's the bigger issue. With better tracks and controls this could have been an excellent racing game. I used to hate the game when it first came out, but like a couple years ago I gave it another shot and ended up really liking a lot about it, even with it's flaws. Also the soundtrack is fantastic.

4:30 SMB3 tho
Something that always gets me about Donkey Kong Country are the lies about how they digitised the characters, There's even a little clip in this vid showing their wireframe Donkey Kong. Yeah they didn't use and kind of wireframe in the actual game, They did what they did for pretty much every other game on the SNES, They drew 2d sprites. Yes they looked good I wouldnt try to deny that, but all the 'look at our wireframes' Complete bullshit! When making Doom they digitised images from models made of clay. Exactly the same process, The only difference is Nintendo had someone knock up wireframes and claimed it made a difference to a game that doesnt use them at all. Again yeah it looks good, But it would have been exactly the same technique had they digitised 2d images, clay models, photos, film footage, hand drawn images. They literally showed the world a 3d Donkey Kong made on an SGI machine (Same machines they made Terminator 2 and Jurassic Park on) and then lied that it was what was going to be used on a SNES, The best part is people still believe it.

HES BACK
As someone who bought and kinda enjoyed Barrel Blast...this...was not the review I was expecting, but it WAS fair! I think the one thing about the reviews at the time that pissed me off was how much people claimed this game was bad because of "rubber banding". My friend lapped the end boss twice. WHY did I buy it? I got a Wii on launch day and needed games. The first year of the Wii was rough. I remember grabbing this and Chicken Little: Ace in Action around the same time mostly out of desperation. The fact that it was made for Bongos only to have the Bongos removed annoyed me, but I do get it due to the control scheme (how do you do a wild move on the bongos). But yeah it was mostly a salvage job: We're too far along in the game's development to scrap it. I did like the different menu animations and some of the new Kremlings were neat. But I was always annoyed that Candy wasn't playable. She's IN the game. You gave her breast physics even! But nope. No playable Candy. Playable Wrinkly? Sure! Playable Candy? NOPE!  ...and then yeah I spent countless hours trying to get to the bottom of Tiny's redesign. Long story short, it's a communication error between the fans and Rare and then between Japan and the US. Tiny being Dixie's little sister was a detail added to DK64 at the last minute due to fan backlash at Rare adding more freaking Kongs and as such it was only ever mentioned in the instruction book. This detail was never translated into the Japanese instruction book so no one in Japan knew Tiny was Dixie's little sister so based on her vague portrayal in DK64 (which involved a bit more hip swinging than it should have) they...decided on THAT for her new more unified look. Not that I'm complaining.

I just re-watched the ending montage and just picked up on the fact that it switched from Breakout to the new theme halfway through. This might very well be the beginning of the end for that song. For the record, that is perfectly fine and it's probably a good decision to not tie your series to a preexisting thing, but still it's gonna be hard to let Breakout go. I also personally think the new theme might lack the versatility of Breakout. Granted we haven't seen much yet, but so far it just sounds like punchy action music and I'm not sure how it would be adapted to other styles. Breakout could easily go from punchy action to dramatic to calm and cheerful. I should give them the time to see what they can do with the theme but so far, it just doesn't seem to have what Breakout has. Or I'm just stubborn and resistant to change. Either way, I'm going to miss Breakout if it is truly gone and willing to give this new theme a shot.  P.S. does the new theme have a name? I feel weird just calling it, "The New Theme".
